<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_belt">Green belt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Green belt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/North_East_Green_Belt" title="North East Green Belt">North East Green Belt</a></div>
<p>The city is within the centre of the wider Tyne &amp; Wear Green Belt,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> with its portion in much of its rural area. It is a part of the local <a href="/wiki/Development_plan" title="Development plan">development plan</a> which is in conjunction with Gateshead borough, and was created in the 1960s.<br />
</p><p>Its stated aims<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> are to:
</p>
<ul><li><i>Prevent the merging of settlements, particularly... Newcastle with Ponteland, or <a href="/wiki/Cramlington" title="Cramlington">Cramlington</a>; the main built-up area with nearby villages; and villages with each other,</i> <br /></li>
<li><i>Safeguard the countryside from encroachment,</i></li>
<li><i>Check unrestricted urban sprawl, and</i></li>
<li><i>Assist in urban regeneration in the city-region by encouraging the recycling of derelict and other urban land.</i></li></ul>
<p>In the Newcastle city boundaries it surrounds the communities of Brunswick Green, <a href="/wiki/Dinnington,_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Dinnington, Tyne and Wear">Dinnington</a>, Callerton, <a href="/wiki/Hazlerigg" title="Hazlerigg">Hazlerigg Village</a>, <a href="/wiki/Throckley" title="Throckley">Throckley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walbottle" title="Walbottle">Walbottle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Woolsington" title="Woolsington">Woolsington</a>. Landscape features and facilities such as Ryton Island, Tyne Riverside Country Park, the city's golf courses, Newcastle Racecourse, and Newcastle Airport are also within the green belt area.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_based_in_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="List of companies based in Newcastle upon Tyne">List of companies based in Newcastle upon Tyne</a></div>
<p>Newcastle played a major role during the 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, and was a leading centre for coal mining, ship building, engineering, munitions and manufacturing. <a href="/wiki/Heavy_industry" title="Heavy industry">Heavy industries</a> in Newcastle declined in the second half of the 20th century; with office, service and retail employment now becoming the city's staples. The city was recognised for its commitment to environmental issues, with a programme planned for Newcastle to become "the first Carbon Neutral town"<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> however those plans have slipped considerably and they now hope to be carbon neutral by 2050<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Newcastle is the commercial, educational and, in partnership with nearby <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>, the cultural focus for <a href="/wiki/North_East_England" title="North East England">North East England</a>. As part of Tyneside, Newcastle's economy contributes around £13&#160;billion to the UK <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">GVA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RegionalGVA_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RegionalGVA-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The Central Business District is in the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne_City_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle upon Tyne City Centre">centre of the city</a>, bounded by <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Haymarket" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle Haymarket">Haymarket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle station</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Quayside" title="Quayside">Quayside</a> areas.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retail">Retail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Retail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg/220px-Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg/330px-Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg/440px-Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northumberland_Street_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1134691.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking north along <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Street" title="Northumberland Street">Northumberland Street</a> in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>In 2010, Newcastle was positioned ninth in the retail centre expenditure league of the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> There are several major shopping areas in <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_City_Centre" title="Newcastle City Centre">Newcastle City Centre</a>. The largest of these is the <a href="/wiki/Eldon_Square_Shopping_Centre" title="Eldon Square Shopping Centre">Eldon Square Shopping Centre</a>, one of the largest city centre shopping complexes in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Eldon_Square2010-07-26_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eldon_Square2010-07-26-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> It incorporates a <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a> store as well as one of the largest <a href="/wiki/John_Lewis_Newcastle" class="mw-redirect" title="John Lewis Newcastle">John Lewis</a> stores in the UK. This John Lewis branch was formerly known as Bainbridges. Newcastle store <a href="/wiki/Bainbridge_(department_store)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bainbridge (department store)">Bainbridge's</a>, opened in 1838, is often cited as the world's first <a href="/wiki/Department_store" title="Department store">department store</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bain20130101_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bain20130101-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Emerson Bainbridge (1817–1892),<sup id="cite_ref-Bain2013102_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bain2013102-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> a pioneer and the founder of Bainbridges,<sup id="cite_ref-Bain2013103_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bain2013103-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> sold goods via department, a new for merchant custom for that time. The Bainbridge's official ledgers reported revenue by department, giving birth to the name department store.<sup id="cite_ref-Bain2013102_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bain2013102-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bain2013103_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bain2013103-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Eldon Square is currently undergoing a full redevelopment. A new bus station, replacing the old underground bus station, was officially opened in March 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The wing of the centre, including the undercover Green Market, near Grainger Street was demolished in 2007 so that the area could be redeveloped.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> This was completed in February 2010 with the opening of a <a href="/wiki/Debenhams" title="Debenhams">Debenhams</a> department store as well as other major stores including <a href="/wiki/Apple_store" class="mw-redirect" title="Apple store">Apple</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hollister_Co." title="Hollister Co.">Hollister</a> and <a href="/wiki/Guess_(clothing)" title="Guess (clothing)">Guess</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main shopping street in the city is <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Street" title="Northumberland Street">Northumberland Street</a>. In a 2004 report, it was ranked as the most expensive shopping street in the UK for rent, outside London.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> It is home to two major department stores including the first and largest <a href="/wiki/Fenwick_(department_store)" title="Fenwick (department store)">Fenwick</a> department store, which houses some of the most luxurious <a href="/wiki/Designer_labels" class="mw-redirect" title="Designer labels">designer labels</a>, and one of the largest <a href="/wiki/Marks_and_Spencer" class="mw-redirect" title="Marks and Spencer">Marks and Spencer</a> stores outside London. Both stores have entrances into Eldon Square Shopping Centre.
</p><p>Other shopping destinations in Newcastle include Grainger Street and the area around <a href="/wiki/Grey%27s_Monument" title="Grey&#39;s Monument">Grey's Monument</a>, the relatively modern Eldon Garden and <a href="/wiki/Monument_Mall" title="Monument Mall">Monument Mall</a> complexes, the Newgate Centre, <a href="/wiki/Central_Arcade" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Arcade">Central Arcade</a> and the traditional <a href="/wiki/Grainger_Market" class="mw-redirect" title="Grainger Market">Grainger Market</a>. Outside the city centre, the largest suburban shopping areas are <a href="/wiki/Gosforth" title="Gosforth">Gosforth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byker" title="Byker">Byker</a>. The largest <a href="/wiki/Tesco" title="Tesco">Tesco</a> store in the United Kingdom is located in <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Park" title="Kingston Park">Kingston Park</a> on the edge of Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
Close to Newcastle, the largest indoor shopping centre in Europe, the <a href="/wiki/MetroCentre_(shopping_centre)" title="MetroCentre (shopping centre)">MetroCentre</a>, is located in Gateshead.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dwelling_types">Dwelling types</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dwelling types">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tyneside_flat" title="Tyneside flat">Tyneside flat</a> was the dominant housing form constructed at the time when the industrial centres on Tyneside were growing most rapidly. They can still be found in areas such as South Heaton in Newcastle but once dominated the streetscape on both sides of the Tyne.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Tyneside flats were built as terraces, one of each pair of doors led to an upstairs flat while the other led into the ground-floor flat, each of two or three rooms. A new development in the Ouseburn valley has recreated them; Architects Cany Ash and Robert Sakula were attracted by the possibilities of high density without building high and getting rid of common areas.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In terms of housing stock, the authority is one of few authorities to see the proportion of detached homes rise in the 2010 Census (to 7.8%), in this instance this was coupled with a similar rise in flats and waterside apartments to 25.6%, and the proportion of converted or shared houses in 2011 renders this dwelling type within the highest of the five colour-coded brackets at 5.9%, and on a par with <a href="/wiki/Oxford" title="Oxford">Oxford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reading,_Berkshire" title="Reading, Berkshire">Reading</a>, greater than <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a> and below a handful of historic densely occupied, arguably overinflated markets in the local authorities: <a href="/wiki/Harrogate" title="Harrogate">Harrogate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cheltenham" title="Cheltenham">Cheltenham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bath,_Somerset" title="Bath, Somerset">Bath</a>, inner London, <a href="/wiki/Hastings" title="Hastings">Hastings</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brighton" title="Brighton">Brighton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Tunbridge_Wells" title="Royal Tunbridge Wells">Royal Tunbridge Wells</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demography">Demography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG/220px-NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG/330px-NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG/440px-NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NE-Westgate_Road_9001.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>West Road Shopping Area in Newcastle's West End has a large multi-ethnic community.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG/220px-NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG/330px-NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG/440px-NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NE-Arthur%27s_Hill_Stanhope_Street_8965.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stanhope Street in Arthur's Hill area is home to the North East's largest Asian community.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg/220px-Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg/330px-Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg/440px-Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gosforth_High_Street_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gosforth High Street in the north of the city.</div></div></div>
<p>According to the ONS in 2015 the city of Newcastle had a population of 293,000.<sup id="cite_ref-pop2015_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop2015-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The metropolitan boroughs of <a href="/wiki/North_Tyneside" title="North Tyneside">North Tyneside</a> (population circa 202,000), <a href="/wiki/South_Tyneside" title="South Tyneside">South Tyneside</a> (population circa 149,000) and <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a> (population circa 201,000)<sup id="cite_ref-pop2015_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop2015-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> are, along with Newcastle, all part of the <a href="/wiki/Tyneside" title="Tyneside">Tyneside</a> <a href="/wiki/Conurbation" title="Conurbation">conurbation</a> (population circa 880,000).<sup id="cite_ref-pop_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The metropolitan county of <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear" title="Tyne and Wear">Tyne and Wear</a>, which consists of the four aforementioned boroughs as well as <a href="/wiki/City_of_Sunderland" title="City of Sunderland">Sunderland</a> (population circa 277,000), had a population of around 1,122,000 and the <a href="/wiki/City_Region_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="City Region (United Kingdom)">Tyne and Wear City Region</a> which also includes North Durham, South East Northumberland and the Tyne Valley has a population of 1,650,000.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Newcastle is also home to a large student population with Newcastle University and Northumbria University Newcastle, based in the City Centre. Areas of suburban Newcastle with major student populations include Jesmond, Gosforth and Heaton.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the same statistics, the average age of people living in Newcastle is 37.8 (the national average being 38.6). There is a strong presence of <a href="/wiki/Border_Reiver" class="mw-redirect" title="Border Reiver">Border Reiver</a> surnames, such as Armstrong, Charlton, Elliot, Johnstone, Kerr, Hall, Nixon, Little and Robson. There are also small but significant Chinese, Jewish and Eastern European (Polish, Czech Roma) populations. The <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a> states there are estimated to be between 500 and 2,000 <a href="/wiki/Bolivians_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Bolivians in the United Kingdom">Bolivians</a> in Newcastle, one of the largest populations in any city in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BoliviansLondNewcEding_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BoliviansLondNewcEding-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Like most cities, Newcastle has diverse cross sections and classes.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jesm_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jesm-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The city is largely Christian at 70.6%; Muslims form 6.2%,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and over 16% have <a href="/wiki/Irreligion" title="Irreligion">no religion</a>.
</p><p>In 2011, 189,381 people lived in the unparished area of Newcastle upon Tyne but 280,177 people lived in the actual city and metropolitan borough. The unparished area excludes Newburn, Gosforth and the wards of Castle, Woolsington and Parklands and is made up of 17 wards from Walkergate in the east to Benwell and Scotswood in the west.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to 2011 figures,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> the city's ethnic make-up is as follows:
</p>
<ul><li>White British: 81.3%</li>
<li>Asian: 9.7%</li>
<li>White Other: 3%</li>
<li>Black: 2.2%</li>
<li>Mixed-race: 1.6%</li>
<li>Other: 1.5%</li></ul>
<p>White people are 84.3% of the population (81.3% White British, 3.0% White other), Asain people 9.7% of the population (3.4% Pakistani, 2.0% Bangladeshi, 2.0% Indian, 2.0% Chinese, 0.3% other), 2.2% Black British (1.9% Black African, 0.2% Black Caribbean, 0.1% Black other), Mixed Race at 1.6% (1.0% Asian and White, 0.4% White and Caribbean, 0.2% White and African) and other ethnicities composing of 1.5% of the population.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Regional_nickname" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional nickname">regional nickname</a> for people from Newcastle and the surrounding area is <a href="/wiki/Geordie" title="Geordie">Geordie</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> term <i>Novocastrian</i>, which can equally be applied to residents of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Newcastle (disambiguation)">any place called Newcastle</a>, is also used for ex-pupils of the city's <a href="/wiki/Royal_Grammar_School,_Newcastle" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Grammar School, Newcastle">Royal Grammar School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Year and current total population<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
