<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dialect">Dialect</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Dialect">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geordie" title="Geordie">Geordie</a></div>
<p>The dialect of Newcastle is known as <a href="/wiki/Geordie" title="Geordie">Geordie</a>, and contains a large amount of vocabulary and distinctive words and pronunciations not used in other parts of the United Kingdom. The Geordie dialect has much of its origins in the language spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Anglo-Saxon</a> populations who migrated to and conquered much of England after the end of Roman Imperial rule. This language was the forerunner of <a href="/wiki/Modern_English" title="Modern English">Modern English</a>; but while the dialects of other English regions have been heavily altered by the influences of other foreign languages—particularly <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norman_language" title="Norman language">Norman French</a>—the Geordie dialect retains many elements of the old language. An example of this is the pronunciation of certain words: "dead", "cow", "house" and "strong" are pronounced "deed", "coo", "hoos" and "strang"—which is how they were pronounced in the Anglo-Saxon language. Other Geordie words with Anglo-Saxon origins include: "larn" (from the Anglo-Saxon "laeran", meaning "teach"), "burn" ("stream") and "gan" ("go").<sup id="cite_ref-GeordieOrigins_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GeordieOrigins-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>"Bairn" and "hyem", meaning "child" and "home", respectively, are examples of Geordie words with origins in Scandinavia;<sup id="cite_ref-bairnHyemScandinavianOrig_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bairnHyemScandinavianOrig-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> <i>barn</i> and <i>hjem</i> are the corresponding modern Norwegian and Danish words. Some words used in the Geordie dialect are used elsewhere in the Northern United Kingdom. The words "bonny" (meaning "pretty"), "howay" ("come on"), "<a href="/wiki/Stotting" title="Stotting">stot</a>" ("bounce") and "hadaway" ("go away" or "you're kidding"), all appear to be used in <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>; "aye" ("yes") and "nowt" (IPA://naʊt/, rhymes with <i>out</i>, "nothing") are used elsewhere in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a>. Many words, however, appear to be used exclusively in Newcastle and the surrounding area, such as "canny" (a versatile word meaning "good", "nice" or "very"), "hacky" ("dirty"), "netty" ("toilet"), "hoy" ("throw", from the Dutch <i>gooien</i>, via <a href="/wiki/West_Frisian_Dutch" title="West Frisian Dutch">West Frisian</a>), "hockle" ("spit").<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2011 the health of people in Newcastle upon Tyne was generally worse than the England average:<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Deprivation is higher than average and 16,670 children live in poverty.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> for both men and women is lower than the England average. Life expectancy is 14.3 years lower for men and 11.1 years lower for women in some of the most deprived areas of Newcastle upon Tyne than in certain least deprived areas<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>From 2001 to 2011, as with all UK cities all-cause mortality rates have fallen, life expectancy has increased. Early death rates from cancer and from heart disease and stroke have fallen but remain worse than the English average.</li>
<li>About 21.9% of Year 6 children are classified as obese. In 2014/5 35.9% of 10 to 11-year-olds were classified as overweight or obese, in comparison to a national average of 33.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> 54.9% of pupils meet the recommendation of at least three hours each week on school sport. Levels of <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy" title="Teenage pregnancy">teenage pregnancy</a> are worse than the England average. In 2011 <a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSE</a> attainment amongst school children was worse than the England average.<sup id="cite_ref-GCSE_2011_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GCSE_2011-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Estimated levels of adult 'healthy eating' and smoking are worse than the England average.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Rates of smoking related deaths<sup id="cite_ref-Smok2012_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smok2012-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> and hospital stays for alcohol-related harm are higher than average.</li>
<li>Newcastle remains one of the few major cities in England to supply <a href="/wiki/Water_fluoridation" title="Water fluoridation">fluoridated water</a>, this scheme is directed by <a href="/wiki/Northumbrian_Water_Group" title="Northumbrian Water Group">Northumbria Water plc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne_Hospitals_NHS_Foundation_Trust" title="Newcastle upon Tyne Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust">Newcastle upon Tyne Hospitals NHS Foundation Trust</a> has one of the lowest mortality rates in the country and is ranked seventh in the country for confidence in doctors.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Newcastle has two large teaching hospitals: the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Infirmary" title="Royal Victoria Infirmary">Royal Victoria Infirmary</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Freeman_Hospital" title="Freeman Hospital">Freeman Hospital</a>, which is also a pioneering centre for <a href="/wiki/Organ_transplant" class="mw-redirect" title="Organ transplant">transplant surgery</a>.
</p><p>In a report, published in early February 2007 by the Ear Institute at the <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Widex" title="Widex">Widex</a>, a Danish hearing aid manufacturer, Newcastle was named as the noisiest city in the whole of the UK, with an average level of 80.4 <a href="/wiki/Decibel" title="Decibel">decibels</a>. The report claimed that these noise levels would have a negative long-term impact on the health of the city's residents.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> The report was rightly criticised, however, for attaching too much weight to readings at arbitrarily selected locations, which in Newcastle's case included a motorway underpass without pedestrian access.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> As well as numerous parks, open spaces, and extensive riverside areas, puzzlingly the report also overlooked the 1000 acre <a href="/wiki/Town_Moor,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Town Moor, Newcastle upon Tyne">Town Moor</a> at the heart of the city. Larger than London's Hyde Park and Hampstead Heath combined,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> and even larger than New York's <a href="/wiki/Central_Park" title="Central Park">Central Park</a> the town moor dates back to the 12th century, with the land tenure and its use being regulated by an Act of Parliament.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">Nightlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Nightlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Gate_outside_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/The_Gate_outside_4.jpg/220px-The_Gate_outside_4.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/The_Gate_outside_4.jpg/330px-The_Gate_outside_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/The_Gate_outside_4.jpg/440px-The_Gate_outside_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Gate_outside_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Gate complex is a popular nightlife destination in the city with a cinema, numerous restaurants and bars.</div></div></div>
<p>Newcastle was in the top ten of the country's top night spots,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> and <i>The <a href="/wiki/Rough_Guides" title="Rough Guides">Rough Guide</a> to Britain</i> placed Newcastle upon Tyne's nightlife as Great Britain's no. 1 <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">tourist attraction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Tripadvisor" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripadvisor">Tripadvisor</a> Travellers' Choice Destination Awards for European Nightlife destinations, four of the UK's nightspots finished in the top 10; Newcastle was awarded 3rd Place behind London, and Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-tripadvisor2010-08-12_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tripadvisor2010-08-12-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Newcastle also came in seventh for the World category,<sup id="cite_ref-Tripadvisor2-2010-08-12_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tripadvisor2-2010-08-12-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> and is confirmed to have the most events per student population in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are concentrations of pubs, bars and nightclubs around the Bigg Market and the <a href="/wiki/Quayside" title="Quayside">Quayside</a> area of the city centre. There are many bars on the Bigg Market, and other popular areas for nightlife are <a href="/wiki/Cuthbert_Collingwood,_1st_Baron_Collingwood" title="Cuthbert Collingwood, 1st Baron Collingwood">Collingwood</a> Street, popularly referred to as the 'Diamond Strip' due to its concentration of high-end bars, Neville Street, the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle station</a> area and Osborne Road in the <a href="/wiki/Jesmond" title="Jesmond">Jesmond</a> area of the city. In recent years "<a href="/wiki/The_Gate,_Newcastle" title="The Gate, Newcastle">The Gate</a>" has opened in the city centre, a new indoor complex consisting of bars, clubs, restaurants and a 12-screen Cineworld multiplex cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Newcastle's <a href="/wiki/Gay_community" class="mw-redirect" title="Gay community">gay scene</a> – 'The Pink Triangle' – is centred on the Times Square area near the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Life" title="Centre for Life">Centre for Life</a> and has a range of bars, cafés and clubs.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has a wide variety of restaurants such as <a href="/wiki/Italian_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian food">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian food">Indian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Persian food">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japanese_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese food">Japanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek food">Greek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican food">Mexican</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish food">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_food" class="mw-redirect" title="American food">American</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polish_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish food">Polish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysian_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Malaysian food">Malaysian</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_food" class="mw-redirect" title="French food">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_cuisine" title="Mongolian cuisine">Mongolian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan food">Moroccan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_cuisine" title="Thai cuisine">Thai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_cuisine" title="Vietnamese cuisine">Vietnamese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_cuisine" title="Lebanese cuisine">Lebanese</a>. Newcastle is one of 7 cities in the UK that has a <a href="/wiki/Chinatown" title="Chinatown">Chinese village</a> with many <a href="/wiki/Chinese_food" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese food">Chinese restaurants</a> on Stowell Street. There has also been a growth in <a href="/wiki/Gourmet" title="Gourmet">premium</a> restaurants in recent years with top chefs.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre">Theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_(6710178097).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_%286710178097%29.jpg/220px-Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_%286710178097%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_%286710178097%29.jpg/330px-Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_%286710178097%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_%286710178097%29.jpg/440px-Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_%286710178097%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="798" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Theatre_Royal_in_Newcastle_(6710178097).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Theatre Royal, Grey Street</div></div></div>
<p>The city has a proud history of theatre. <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Kemble" title="Stephen Kemble">Stephen Kemble</a> of the famous <a href="/wiki/Kemble_family" title="Kemble family">Kemble family</a> successfully managed the original Theatre Royal, Newcastle for fifteen years (1791–1806). He brought members of his famous acting family such as <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Siddons" title="Sarah Siddons">Sarah Siddons</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Kemble" title="John Philip Kemble">John Kemble</a> out of London to Newcastle. Stephen Kemble guided the theatre through many celebrated seasons. The original Theatre Royal in Newcastle was opened on 21 January 1788 and was located on Mosley Street.<sup id="cite_ref-theatreRoyal1788_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theatreRoyal1788-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> It was demolished to make way for Grey Street, where its replacement was built.
</p><p>The city still contains many theatres. The largest, the <a href="/wiki/Theatre_Royal,_Newcastle" title="Theatre Royal, Newcastle">Theatre Royal</a> on Grey Street, first opened in 1837, designed by <a href="/wiki/John_and_Benjamin_Green" title="John and Benjamin Green">John and Benjamin Green</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-JBGreen_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JBGreen-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> It has hosted a season of performances from the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Shakespeare_Company" title="Royal Shakespeare Company">Royal Shakespeare Company</a> for over 25 years, as well as touring productions of West End musicals.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mill_Volvo_Tyne_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Mill Volvo Tyne Theatre">Mill Volvo Tyne Theatre</a> hosts smaller touring productions, whilst other venues feature local talent. <a href="/wiki/Northern_Stage,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Northern Stage, Newcastle upon Tyne">Northern Stage</a>, formally known as the Newcastle Playhouse and Gulbenkian Studio, hosts various local, national and international productions in addition to those produced by the Northern Stage company.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Other theatres in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Live_Theatre_Company" title="Live Theatre Company">Live Theatre</a>, the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Theatre,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="People&#39;s Theatre, Newcastle upon Tyne">People's Theatre</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://alphabettitheatre.co.uk/">Alphabetti Theatre</a>  and the <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_Theatre" title="Jubilee Theatre">Jubilee Theatre</a>. <a href="/wiki/NewcastleGateshead" title="NewcastleGateshead">NewcastleGateshead</a> was voted in 2006 as the arts capital of the UK in a survey conducted by the <a href="/wiki/Artsworld" class="mw-redirect" title="Artsworld">Artsworld</a> TV channel.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature_and_libraries">Literature and libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Literature and libraries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_City_Library.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Newcastle_City_Library.jpg/200px-Newcastle_City_Library.jpg" width="200" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Newcastle_City_Library.jpg/300px-Newcastle_City_Library.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Newcastle_City_Library.jpg/400px-Newcastle_City_Library.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3891" data-file-height="3119" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_City_Library.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Avison Library 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Newcastle has a strong reputation as a poetry centre. The <a href="/wiki/Morden_Tower" title="Morden Tower">Morden Tower</a>, run by poet <a href="/wiki/Tom_Pickard" title="Tom Pickard">Tom Pickard</a>, is a major venue for poetry readings in the North East, being the place where <a href="/wiki/Basil_Bunting" title="Basil Bunting">Basil Bunting</a> gave the first reading of <i><a href="/wiki/Briggflatts" title="Briggflatts">Briggflatts</a></i> in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Literary_and_Philosophical_Society_of_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Literary and Philosophical Society of Newcastle upon Tyne">Literary and Philosophical Society of Newcastle upon Tyne</a> (popularly known as the 'Lit &amp; Phil') is the largest independent library outside London, housing more than 150,000 books. Its music library contains 8,000 CDs and 10,000 LPs.<sup id="cite_ref-litandPhil20110208_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-litandPhil20110208-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Litandphilorguk_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Litandphilorguk-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The current Lit and Phil premises were built in 1825 and the building was designed by John and Benjamin Green.<sup id="cite_ref-JBGreen_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JBGreen-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Operating since 1793 and founded as a 'conversation club,' its lecture theatre was the first public building to be lit by electric light, during a lecture by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Swan" title="Joseph Swan">Joseph Swan</a> on 20 October 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-litandPhil20110208_169-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-litandPhil20110208-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The old City library designed by <a href="/wiki/Basil_Spence" title="Basil Spence">Basil Spence</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BasilSpence_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BasilSpence-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> was demolished in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-BasilSpence_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BasilSpence-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> and replaced. The new building opened on 21 June 2009<sup id="cite_ref-AvisonLibrary_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvisonLibrary-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> and was named after 18th century composer <a href="/wiki/Charles_Avison" title="Charles Avison">Charles Avison</a>; the building was opened by <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Loebl" title="Herbert Loebl">Dr Herbert Loebl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AvisonLibrary_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AvisonLibrary-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Seven_Stories" title="Seven Stories">Seven Stories</a> is a museum dedicated to children's books. Opened in 2005, it is based in the <a href="/wiki/Ouseburn_Valley" title="Ouseburn Valley">Ouseburn Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sstories201102_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sstories201102-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2010_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2010-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals_and_fairs">Festivals and fairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Festivals and fairs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg/220px-Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg/330px-Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg/440px-Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chinatown_Arch_Newcastle_UK.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The arch to Chinatown, opposite St. James' Park</div></div></div>
<p>In January or February, <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Newcastle" title="Chinatown, Newcastle">Newcastle's Chinatown</a> is at the centre of a carnival of colour and noise as the city celebrates the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a>.
In early March there is the <a href="/wiki/NewcastleGateshead" title="NewcastleGateshead">NewcastleGateshead</a> Comedy Festival. This event makes a return to the region since the last event in 2006. It is hoped it will now continue as an annual event.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The Newcastle Science Festival, now called <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_ScienceFest" title="Newcastle ScienceFest">Newcastle ScienceFest</a>, returns annually in early March.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Newcastle <a href="/wiki/Beer_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Beer Festival">Beer Festival</a>, organised by <a href="/wiki/Campaign_for_Real_Ale" title="Campaign for Real Ale">CAMRA</a>, takes place in April.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Evolution_Festival" title="Evolution Festival">Evolution Festival</a>, a music festival that attracted tens of thousands of attendees, took place in May from 2002 until 2013 and was described as "the biggest festival Tyneside has ever staged".<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The This Is Tomorrow festival now takes place over the spring bank holiday and is in the same location. The biennial <a href="/wiki/AV_Festival" title="AV Festival">AV Festival</a> of international electronic art, featuring exhibitions, concerts, conferences and film screenings, is held in March. The North East Art Expo, a festival of art and design from the regions professional artists, is held in late May.<sup id="cite_ref-artExpo2_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artExpo2-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-artExpoNe1_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-artExpoNe1-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> EAT! NewcastleGateshead, a festival of food and drink, runs for 2 weeks each year in mid June.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/The_Hoppings" title="The Hoppings">The Hoppings</a>, reputedly the largest travelling fair in Europe, takes place on <a href="/wiki/Town_Moor,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Town Moor, Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle Town Moor</a> every June. The event has its origins in the <a href="/wiki/Temperance_movement_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Temperance movement in the United Kingdom">Temperance Movement</a> during the early 1880s, and coincides with the annual <a href="/wiki/Horse_racing" title="Horse racing">race week</a> at High Gosforth Park.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> Newcastle Community Green Festival, which claims to be the UK's biggest free community <a href="/wiki/Environmental_science" title="Environmental science">environmental</a> festival, also takes place every June, in <a href="/wiki/Leazes_Park" title="Leazes Park">Leazes Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The Northern Rock Cyclone, a cycling festival, takes place within, or starting from, Newcastle in June.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The Northern Pride Festival and Parade is held in <a href="/wiki/Leazes_Park" title="Leazes Park">Leazes Park</a> and in the city's Gay Community in mid July. The Ouseburn Festival, a family oriented weekend festival near the city centre, incorporating a "Family Fun Day" and "Carnival Day", is held in late July.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Newcastle <a href="/wiki/Mela" title="Mela">Mela</a>, held on the late <a href="/wiki/August_Bank_Holiday" class="mw-redirect" title="August Bank Holiday">August Bank Holiday</a> weekend, is an annual two-day multicultural event that blends drama, music and food from <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_culture#Modern_Punjabi_Culture" title="Punjabi culture">Punjabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Pakistan" title="Culture of Pakistan">Pakistani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengal#Culture" title="Bengal">Bengali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> NewcastleGateshead also holds an annual International Arts Fair. The 2009 event will be in the <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster,_Baron_Foster_of_Thames_Bank" title="Norman Foster, Baron Foster of Thames Bank">Norman Foster</a> designed <a href="/wiki/Sage_Gateshead" title="Sage Gateshead">Sage Gateshead</a> Music and Arts Centre in September.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In October, there is the Design Event festival—an annual festival providing the public with an opportunity to see work by regional, national and international designers.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
The SAMA Festival, an East Asian cultural festival is also held in early October.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg/260px-Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg/390px-Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg/520px-Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="867" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sting_by_Yancho_Sabev.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>, principal songwriter, lead singer and bassist for English rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Police" title="The Police">The Police</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_bands_and_musicians_from_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="List of bands and musicians from Newcastle Upon Tyne">List of bands and musicians from Newcastle Upon Tyne</a></div>
<p>Newcastle's vernacular music was a mixture of Northumbrian <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk music</a> and nineteenth-century songs with dialect lyrics, by writers such as <a href="/wiki/George_%22Geordie%22_Ridley" title="George &quot;Geordie&quot; Ridley">George "Geordie" Ridley</a>, whose songs include one which became an unofficial Tyneside national anthem, <a href="/wiki/Blaydon_Races" title="Blaydon Races">Blaydon Races</a>.
</p><p>The 1960s saw the internationally successful rock group <a href="/wiki/The_Animals" title="The Animals">The Animals</a>, emerge from Newcastle night spots such as Club A-Go-Go<sup id="cite_ref-Theanimals1962ClubAGogo_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Theanimals1962ClubAGogo-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> on Percy Street. Other well-known acts with connections to the city include <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Sting2010-08-15_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sting2010-08-15-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Ferry" title="Bryan Ferry">Bryan Ferry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ferry2010-08-15_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ferry2010-08-15-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a><sup id="cite_ref-Direstraits2010-08-15_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Direstraits2010-08-15-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> and more recently <a href="/wiki/Max%C3%AFmo_Park" title="Maxïmo Park">Maxïmo Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Maximo2010-08-15_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maximo2010-08-15-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> There is also a thriving <a href="/wiki/Underground_music" title="Underground music">underground music</a> scene that encompasses a variety of styles, including <a href="/wiki/Drum_and_bass" title="Drum and bass">drum and bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doom_metal" title="Doom metal">doom metal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Post-rock" title="Post-rock">post-rock</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg/260px-Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg/390px-Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg/520px-Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3360" data-file-height="2240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mark_Knopfler_Zwolle_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Dire_Straits" title="Dire Straits">Dire Straits</a> frontman <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a>. His song "<a href="/wiki/Local_Hero_(album)" title="Local Hero (album)">Local Hero</a>" is played at St. James Park before the start of every <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle United">Newcastle United</a> home game.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcastle_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcastle-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Lindisfarne_(band)" title="Lindisfarne (band)">Lindisfarne</a> are a folk-rock group with a strong <a href="/wiki/Tyneside" title="Tyneside">Tyneside</a> connection. Their most famous song, "<a href="/wiki/Fog_on_the_Tyne" title="Fog on the Tyne">Fog on the Tyne</a>" (1971), was covered by <a href="/wiki/Geordie" title="Geordie">Geordie</a> ex-footballer <a href="/wiki/Paul_Gascoigne" title="Paul Gascoigne">Paul Gascoigne</a> in 1990. <a href="/wiki/Venom_(band)" title="Venom (band)">Venom</a>, reckoned by many to be the originators of <a href="/wiki/Black_metal" title="Black metal">black metal</a> and extremely influential to the <a href="/wiki/Extreme_metal" title="Extreme metal">extreme metal</a> scene as a whole, formed in Newcastle in 1979. <a href="/wiki/Folk_metal" title="Folk metal">Folk metal</a> band <a href="/wiki/Skyclad_(band)" title="Skyclad (band)">Skyclad</a>, often regarded as the first folk metal band, also formed in Newcastle after the break-up of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Walkyier" title="Martin Walkyier">Martin Walkyier</a> thrash metal band, <a href="/wiki/Sabbat_(English_band)" title="Sabbat (English band)">Sabbat</a>. <a href="/wiki/Andy_Taylor_(guitarist)" title="Andy Taylor (guitarist)">Andy Taylor</a>, former lead guitarist of <a href="/wiki/Duran_Duran" title="Duran Duran">Duran Duran</a> was born here in 1961. <a href="/wiki/Brian_Johnson" title="Brian Johnson">Brian Johnson</a> was a member of local rock band <a href="/wiki/Geordie_(band)" title="Geordie (band)">Geordie</a> before becoming the lead vocalist of <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a>.
</p><p>Newcastle is the home of <a href="/wiki/Kitchenware_Records" title="Kitchenware Records">Kitchenware Records</a> (c. 1982),<sup id="cite_ref-Kitchenware2010-08-15_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitchenware2010-08-15-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> previously home to acclaimed bands such as <a href="/wiki/Prefab_Sprout" title="Prefab Sprout">Prefab Sprout</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martin_Stephenson_and_the_Daintees" title="Martin Stephenson and the Daintees">Martin Stephenson and the Daintees</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Fatima_Mansions" title="The Fatima Mansions">The Fatima Mansions</a>, the management of <a href="/wiki/The_Lighthouse_Family" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lighthouse Family">The Lighthouse Family</a> and home to recent successes Editors and <a href="/wiki/Sirens_(UK_band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sirens (UK band)">Sirens</a>.
</p><p>The 1990s boom in <a href="/wiki/Progressive_house" title="Progressive house">progressive house</a> music saw the city's <a href="/wiki/Global_Underground" title="Global Underground">Global Underground</a> record label publish mix CDs by the likes of <a href="/wiki/Sasha_(DJ)" title="Sasha (DJ)">Sasha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Oakenfold" title="Paul Oakenfold">Paul Oakenfold</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Lavelle" title="James Lavelle">James Lavelle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Danny_Howells" title="Danny Howells">Danny Howells</a> recording mix compilations. The label is still going strong today with offices in London and New York, and new releases from <a href="/wiki/Deep_Dish_(band)" title="Deep Dish (band)">Deep Dish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Freeland" title="Adam Freeland">Adam Freeland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Newcastle's leading classical music ensemble is the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Northern_Sinfonia" title="Royal Northern Sinfonia">Royal Northern Sinfonia</a>, which was founded in 1958 and performed regularly at Newcastle City Hall until 2004. Nowadays it is based at <a href="/wiki/The_Sage_Gateshead" class="mw-redirect" title="The Sage Gateshead">The Sage, Gateshead</a>.
</p><p>ICMuS, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a>'s music department, has been a driving force for music in the region, producing innovative work, organising concerts and festivals, instigating the first degree programme in folk music in the British Isles, and engaging creatively with communities in the region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Concert_venues">Concert venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Concert venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Metroradio_Arena,_Newcastle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Metroradio_Arena%2C_Newcastle.jpg/220px-Metroradio_Arena%2C_Newcastle.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Metroradio_Arena%2C_Newcastle.jpg/330px-Metroradio_Arena%2C_Newcastle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Metroradio_Arena%2C_Newcastle.jpg/440px-Metroradio_Arena%2C_Newcastle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Metroradio_Arena,_Newcastle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Metro Radio Arena</div></div></div>
<p>The largest venue used for music concerts is St James Park, home of Newcastle United, which has also previously been used for Rugby League games and the Olympic Games. The second largest <a href="/wiki/Music_venue" title="Music venue">music venue</a> in Newcastle is the 11,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Metro_Radio_Arena_Newcastle" class="mw-redirect" title="Metro Radio Arena Newcastle">Metro Radio Arena</a>, which opened in 1995 and hosts major pop and rock concerts.<sup id="cite_ref-indthrive_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indthrive-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_City_Hall" title="Newcastle City Hall">Newcastle City Hall</a> is one of the oldest venues in the region and "attracts big names who are often legends of the past".<sup id="cite_ref-indthrive_199-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indthrive-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Both of the city's universities have venues that mainly host <a href="/wiki/Indie_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Indie music">indie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alternative_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternative music">alternative</a> bands.<sup id="cite_ref-indthrive_199-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indthrive-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 October 2005 the 2,000 capacity <a href="/wiki/O2_Academy_Newcastle" title="O2 Academy Newcastle">O2 Academy Newcastle</a> opened in the city centre. It had previously been a music venue in the 1960s, hosting concerts by <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Who" title="The Who">The Who</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-o2academy_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-o2academy-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> The new venue was headlined by <a href="/wiki/The_Futureheads" title="The Futureheads">The Futureheads</a> on the opening night and known as the Carling Academy for a number of years. Since opening the venue has hosted performances by major bands and solo musicians including <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Monkeys" title="Arctic Monkeys">Arctic Monkeys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Libertines" title="The Libertines">The Libertines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blondie_(band)" title="Blondie (band)">Blondie</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse" title="Amy Winehouse">Amy Winehouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-lookbig_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lookbig-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Riverside_(music_venue)" title="Riverside (music venue)">Riverside</a> music venue on Melbourne Street, open from 1985 until 1999, famously hosted <a href="/wiki/Nirvana_(band)" title="Nirvana (band)">Nirvana</a>'s first European show in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The venue also welcomed <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Bowie" title="David Bowie">David Bowie</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Stone_Roses" title="The Stone Roses">The Stone Roses</a> and was named Best Regional Venue by <a href="/wiki/New_Musical_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="New Musical Express">NME</a> in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Riverside has also been the subject of a book, <i>Riverside: Newcastle's Legendary Alternative Music Venue</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016 open-air concerts will take place at Times Square for the first time, including performances from <a href="/wiki/Max%C3%AFmo_Park" title="Maxïmo Park">Maxïmo Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Colour_Scene" title="Ocean Colour Scene">Ocean Colour Scene</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catfish_and_the_Bottlemen" title="Catfish and the Bottlemen">Catfish and the Bottlemen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The small music venue Think Tank? was a nominee for Best Small Venue in NME in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Cluny" title="The Cluny">The Cluny</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ouseburn_Valley" title="Ouseburn Valley">Ouseburn Valley</a> is "one of the most important venues for breaking bands in the region".<sup id="cite_ref-evoemergingvenues_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evoemergingvenues-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Trillians Rock Bar is well-noted for its rock and <a href="/wiki/Metal_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Metal music">metal</a> shows,<sup id="cite_ref-indthrive_199-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-indthrive-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> and The Head of Steam is a 90-capacity basement venue described as "one of Newcastle's staple venues".<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tyneside_Cinema,_Feb_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tyneside_Cinema%2C_Feb_2010.jpg/200px-Tyneside_Cinema%2C_Feb_2010.jpg" width="200" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tyneside_Cinema%2C_Feb_2010.jpg/300px-Tyneside_Cinema%2C_Feb_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Tyneside_Cinema%2C_Feb_2010.jpg/400px-Tyneside_Cinema%2C_Feb_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1139" data-file-height="1664" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tyneside_Cinema,_Feb_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tyneside_Cinema" title="Tyneside Cinema">Tyneside Cinema</a>, designed and built by Dixon Scott, great uncle of <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony Scott</a><sup id="cite_ref-RidTonScottcinema_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidTonScottcinema-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Apart from the city centre chain-cinema, the <a href="/wiki/Empire_Cinemas" title="Empire Cinemas">Empire</a> multiplex, the city has its own independent cinema, the <a href="/wiki/Tyneside_Cinema" title="Tyneside Cinema">Tyneside Cinema</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The Tyneside Cinema, on Pilgrim Street, originally opened as the 'Bijou News-Reel Cinema' in 1937, and was designed and built by Dixon Scott, great-uncle of film directors <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a><sup id="cite_ref-RidTonScottcinema_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RidTonScottcinema-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tony_Scott" title="Tony Scott">Tony Scott</a>.
</p><p>The Pilgrim Street building was refurbished between November 2006 and May 2008; during the refurbishment works, the cinema relocated to the Old Town Hall, Gateshead. In May 2008 the Tyneside Cinema reopened in the restored and refurbished original building.<sup id="cite_ref-tynescinem_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynescinem-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The site currently houses three cinemas, including the restored Classic<sup id="cite_ref-tynesidecinclassic_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tynesidecinclassic-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> —the United Kingdom's last surviving news cinema still in full-time operation—alongside two new screens, and dedicated education and teaching suites.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_galleries">Museums and galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Museums and galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are several museums and galleries in Newcastle, including the <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Life" title="Centre for Life">Centre for Life</a><sup id="cite_ref-centerlife201102_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-centerlife201102-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> with its Science Village;<sup id="cite_ref-science_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-science-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Discovery_Museum" title="Discovery Museum">Discovery Museum</a><sup id="cite_ref-discmus201102_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-discmus201102-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> a museum highlighting life on Tyneside, including Tyneside's shipbuilding heritage, and inventions which changed the world; the <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Museum" title="Great North Museum">Great North Museum</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-GreatNorth201102_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GreatNorth201102-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> in 2009 the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Antiquities" title="Museum of Antiquities">Newcastle on Tyne Museum of Antiquities</a> merged with the Great North Museum (Hancock Museum);<sup id="cite_ref-MusAntiquities_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MusAntiquities-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Seven_Stories" title="Seven Stories">Seven Stories</a> a museum dedicated to children's books,<sup id="cite_ref-sstories201102_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sstories201102-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wilson2010_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson2010-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> the Side Gallery historical and contemporary photography from around the world and Northern England<sup id="cite_ref-SideGallery201311_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SideGallery201311-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> and the Newburn Hall Motor Museum.<sup id="cite_ref-NewbH20110223_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewbH20110223-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Laing Art Gallery, like other art galleries and museums around the world, has collections digitised on the <a href="/wiki/Google_Cultural_Institute" title="Google Cultural Institute">Google Cultural Institute</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CulturalInstitute20131217_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CulturalInstitute20131217-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CulturalInstitute201312172_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CulturalInstitute201312172-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> an initiative that makes important cultural material accessible online.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_film">In film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: In film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Films_set_in_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Category:Films set in Newcastle upon Tyne">Category:Films set in Newcastle upon Tyne</a></div>
<p>The earliest known movie featuring some exterior scenes filmed in the city is <i><a href="/wiki/On_the_Night_of_the_Fire" title="On the Night of the Fire">On the Night of the Fire</a></i> (1939),<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> though by and large the action is studio-bound. Later came <i><a href="/wiki/The_Clouded_Yellow" title="The Clouded Yellow">The Clouded Yellow</a></i> (1951) and <i><a href="/wiki/Payroll_(film)" title="Payroll (film)">Payroll</a></i> (1961), both of which feature more extensive scenes filmed in the city. The gangster thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Get_Carter" title="Get Carter">Get Carter</a></i> (1971) was shot on location in and around Newcastle and offers an opportunity to see what Newcastle looked like in the early 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-Get_Carter_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Get_Carter-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> The city was also backdrop to another gangster film, the <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Stormy_Monday_(film)" title="Stormy Monday (film)">Stormy Monday</a></i> (1988), directed by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Figgis" title="Mike Figgis">Mike Figgis</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lee_Jones" title="Tommy Lee Jones">Tommy Lee Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melanie_Griffith" title="Melanie Griffith">Melanie Griffith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sean_Bean" title="Sean Bean">Sean Bean</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sting2010-07-04_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sting2010-07-04-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has been the setting for films based around football; films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Purely_Belter" title="Purely Belter">Purely Belter</a></i> (2000),<sup id="cite_ref-Purely_Belter1_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Purely_Belter1-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_One_and_Only_(2002_film)" title="The One and Only (2002 film)">The One and Only</a></i> (2002)<sup id="cite_ref-The_One_and_Only_2010-07-04_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_One_and_Only_2010-07-04-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/Goal!_(film)" title="Goal! (film)">Goal!</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Goal_2010-07-04_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Goal_2010-07-04-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> have all been focused around Tyneside. The comedy <i><a href="/wiki/School_for_Seduction" title="School for Seduction">School for Seduction</a></i> (2004), starring <a href="/wiki/Kelly_Brook" title="Kelly Brook">Kelly Brook</a> was also filmed in Newcastle.<sup id="cite_ref-SchoolFor_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SchoolFor-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bollywood" title="Bollywood">Bollywood</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Hum_Tum_Aur_Ghost" title="Hum Tum Aur Ghost">Hum Tum Aur Ghost</a></i> (2010) was shot on location in Newcastle's city centre and features key scenes in and around <a href="/wiki/Grainger_Town" title="Grainger Town">Grainger Town</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HumTumAurGhost_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HumTumAurGhost-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The film <i><a href="/wiki/Public_Sex_(film)" title="Public Sex (film)">Public Sex</a></i> (2009) was shot in and around Newcastle, and features several scenes under and around the Tyne Bridge.
</p><p>Crime drama <i>Harrigan</i> (2013) was filmed in the city as well as Gateshead and Teesside.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Television_shows_set_in_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Category:Television shows set in Newcastle upon Tyne">Category:Television shows set in Newcastle upon Tyne</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_James%27_Park,_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/St_James%27_Park%2C_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg/220px-St_James%27_Park%2C_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/St_James%27_Park%2C_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg/330px-St_James%27_Park%2C_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/St_James%27_Park%2C_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg/440px-St_James%27_Park%2C_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_James%27_Park,_view_across_Newcastle_University_to_Civic_Centre_and_beyond_-_geograph.org.uk_-_2689641.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inside St. James' Park – home of Newcastle United Football Club – looking towards the city centre.</div></div></div>
<p>The city has a strong sporting tradition. <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> club <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a> has been based at <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James&#39; Park">St James' Park</a> since the club was established in 1892, although any traces of the original structure are now long gone as the stadium now holds more than 52,000 seated spectators, being England's seventh largest football stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc360_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc360-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> The city also has <a href="/wiki/Non-League_football" title="Non-League football">non-League football</a> clubs, <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Benfield_F.C." title="Newcastle Benfield F.C.">Newcastle Benfield</a>, West Allotment Celtic and Team Northumbria.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Falcons" title="Newcastle Falcons">Newcastle Falcons</a> are the only <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> team in north-east England to have played in the <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Premiership" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviva Premiership">Aviva Premiership</a>. They play at <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Park_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingston Park Stadium">Kingston Park Stadium</a> in the northern suburb of Kingston Park. 1996 Pilkington Shield winners <a href="/wiki/Medicals_RFC" title="Medicals RFC">Medicals RFC</a> are also based in Newcastle.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Thunder" title="Newcastle Thunder">Newcastle Thunder</a> (formerly <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Thunder" title="Newcastle Thunder">Gateshead Thunder</a>) are a professional <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> club based in the city who now also play at <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Park_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingston Park Stadium">Kingston Park Stadium</a>. They currently play in the <a href="/wiki/League_1_(rugby_league)" title="League 1 (rugby league)">Kingstone Press League 1</a>. Since 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> <a href="/wiki/Magic_Weekend" title="Magic Weekend">Magic Weekend</a> has been played annually in the city at St James' Park.
</p><p>There is a women's football team, Newcastle United Women's Football Club, founded in 1989. <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_W.F.C." title="Newcastle United W.F.C.">Newcastle United W.F.C.</a> currently has 40 ladies aged between 16–29 years signed or associated with the club, and plays in the FA Women's Premier League (North).<sup id="cite_ref-nuwfc_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nuwfc-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Newcastle has a <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Racecourse" title="Newcastle Racecourse">horse racing course</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gosforth_Park" title="Gosforth Park">Gosforth Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Horse_racing_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horse_racing-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>
The city is also home to the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Eagles" title="Newcastle Eagles">Newcastle Eagles</a> basketball team who play their home games at the new Sport Central complex at <a href="/wiki/Northumbria_University" title="Northumbria University">Northumbria University</a>. The Eagles are the most successful team in the history of the <a href="/wiki/British_Basketball_League" title="British Basketball League">British Basketball League (BBL)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eagles2014_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eagles2014-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
The city's <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle_speedway" title="Motorcycle speedway">speedway</a> team <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Diamonds" title="Newcastle Diamonds">Newcastle Diamonds</a> are based at Brough Park in <a href="/wiki/Byker" title="Byker">Byker</a>, a venue that is also home to <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_racing" title="Greyhound racing">greyhound racing</a>. Newcastle also hosts the start of the annual <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Run" title="Great North Run">Great North Run</a>, the world's largest <a href="/wiki/Half_marathon" title="Half marathon">half-marathon</a> in which participants race over the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_Bridge" title="Tyne Bridge">Tyne Bridge</a> into <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a> and then towards the finish line 13.1 miles (21.1&#160;km) away on the coast at <a href="/wiki/South_Shields" title="South Shields">South Shields</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> Another famous athletic event is the 5.9-mile (9.5&#160;km) <a href="/wiki/Blaydon_Race" title="Blaydon Race">Blaydon Race</a> (a road race from Newcastle to <a href="/wiki/Blaydon" class="mw-redirect" title="Blaydon">Blaydon</a>), which has taken place on 9 June annually since 1981, to commemorate the celebrated <a href="/wiki/Blaydon_Races" title="Blaydon Races">Blaydon Races</a> horse racing.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The 2012 London Olympic committee selected Newcastle as one of the UK host venue cities,<sup id="cite_ref-olymp11_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olymp11-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-olymp2_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olymp2-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> with the stadium St James' Park hosting 9 matches in both the men's and women's football.<sup id="cite_ref-olymp3_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olymp3-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Warriors" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle Warriors">Newcastle Warriors</a> were a professional <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a> team that played the 1995–96 season in the <a href="/wiki/British_Hockey_League" title="British Hockey League">British Hockey League</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Vipers" title="Newcastle Vipers">Newcastle Vipers</a> were also a professional ice hockey team in the <a href="/wiki/British_National_League_(1996%E2%80%932005)" title="British National League (1996–2005)">British National League</a> from 2002 and then the <a href="/wiki/Elite_Ice_Hockey_League" title="Elite Ice Hockey League">Elite Ice Hockey League</a> between 2005 and 2011 (when the team folded).
</p><p>Newcastle upon Tyne was one of the 11 host cities for the 2015 Rugby World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> St James' Park hosted three matches;
</p>
<ul><li>South Africa v Scotland (3 October 2015)</li>
<li>New Zealand v Tonga (9 October 2015)</li>
<li>Samoa v Scotland (10 October 2015)</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_City_Council" title="Newcastle City Council">Newcastle City Council</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg/220px-Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg/330px-Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg/440px-Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_civiccentre_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Civic_Centre" title="Newcastle Civic Centre">Newcastle Civic Centre</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Northumberland_Fusiliers_Memorial" title="Northumberland Fusiliers Memorial">Northumberland Fusiliers Memorial</a></div></div></div>
<p>Newcastle is governed using the leader and cabinet system, and the executive is <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a>, as they have 55 <a href="/wiki/Councillors" class="mw-redirect" title="Councillors">councillors</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a>' 20. No other parties hold <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">seats</a> on the city's council, but there are 3 independent councillors.
</p><p>For the purposes of City Council elections, Newcastle is divided into 26 <a href="/wiki/Ward_(politics)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ward (politics)">electoral wards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> Following the boundary changes in 2016, the wards are as follows:
</p>

<li><a href="/wiki/Blakelaw" title="Blakelaw">Blakelaw</a></li>
