<p>The Members of parliament are <a href="/wiki/Catherine_McKinnell" title="Catherine McKinnell">Catherine McKinnell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nick_Brown" title="Nick Brown">Nick Brown</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chi_Onwurah" title="Chi Onwurah">Chi Onwurah</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Tyne_and_Wear" title="Transport in Tyne and Wear">Transport in Tyne and Wear</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Airport" title="Newcastle Airport">Newcastle Airport</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg/220px-Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg/330px-Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg/440px-Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aircraft_at_Newcastle_Airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Planes parked at <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Airport" title="Newcastle Airport">Newcastle Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p>Newcastle Airport is located approximately 6 miles (9.7&#160;km) from the city centre on the northern outskirts of the city near <a href="/wiki/Ponteland" title="Ponteland">Ponteland</a> and is the larger of the two main airports serving the North East. It is connected to the city via the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_%26_Wear_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyne &amp; Wear Metro">Tyne &amp; Wear Metro</a> system and a journey into Newcastle city centre takes approximately 20 minutes. The airport handles over five million passengers per year, and is the tenth largest, and the fastest growing regional airport in the UK,<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> expecting to reach 10 million passengers by 2016, and 15&#160;million by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> As of  2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, over 90 destinations are available worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle railway station</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Platforms_2_and_3,_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Platforms_2_and_3%2C_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg/220px-Platforms_2_and_3%2C_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Platforms_2_and_3%2C_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg/330px-Platforms_2_and_3%2C_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Platforms_2_and_3%2C_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg/440px-Platforms_2_and_3%2C_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Platforms_2_and_3,_Newcastle_Central_Station_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1707736.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inside <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle station</a></div></div></div>
<p>Newcastle railway station, also known as Newcastle Central station, is a principal stop on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cross_Country_Route" title="Cross Country Route">Cross Country Route</a>. Newcastle station is one of the busiest stations in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-Portico2014_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portico2014-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, work was completed on the stations historic entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-Portico2014_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portico2014-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Glazing was placed over the historic arches and the Victorian architecture was enhanced; transforming the 19th century public portico.<sup id="cite_ref-Portico2014_248-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portico2014-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> The station is one of only six Grade One listed railway stations in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-Portico2014_248-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portico2014-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> Opened in 1850 by <a href="/wiki/Victoria_of_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Victoria of the United Kingdom">Queen Victoria</a>, it was the first covered railway station in the world and was much copied across the UK. It has a <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> façade, originally designed by the architect John Dobson, and was constructed in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stephenson" title="Robert Stephenson">Robert Stephenson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> The station sightlines towards the Castle Keep, whilst showcasing the curvature of the station's arched roof.<sup id="cite_ref-Portico2014_248-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Portico2014-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> The first services were operated by the <a href="/wiki/North_Eastern_Railway_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="North Eastern Railway (UK)">North Eastern Railway</a> company. The city's other mainline station, <a href="/wiki/Manors_railway_station" title="Manors railway station">Manors</a>, is to the east of the city centre.
</p><p>Train operator <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> provides a half-hourly frequency of trains to <a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King's Cross</a>, with a journey time of about three hours, and north to <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> with all trains calling at <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a> and a small number of trains extended to <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station">Glasgow Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_railway_station" title="Aberdeen railway station">Aberdeen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inverness_railway_station" title="Inverness railway station">Inverness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a> trains serve destinations in <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">Yorkshire</a>, the <a href="/wiki/English_Midlands" class="mw-redirect" title="English Midlands">Midlands</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West</a>. <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> operates services to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool Lime Street</a>. <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> provides local and regional services.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haymarket_-_completion_(platform).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haymarket_-_completion_%28platform%29.JPG/220px-Haymarket_-_completion_%28platform%29.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haymarket_-_completion_%28platform%29.JPG/330px-Haymarket_-_completion_%28platform%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Haymarket_-_completion_%28platform%29.JPG/440px-Haymarket_-_completion_%28platform%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haymarket_-_completion_(platform).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haymarket_Metro_station" title="Haymarket Metro station">Haymarket Metro station</a> in Newcastle city centre</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tyne_%26_Wear_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyne &amp; Wear Metro">Tyne &amp; Wear Metro</a></div>
<p>The city is served by the Tyne &amp; Wear Metro, a system of suburban and underground railways covering much of Tyne &amp; Wear. It was opened in five phases between 1980 and 1984, and was Britain's first urban light rail transit system;<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> two extensions were opened in 1991 and 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> It was developed from a combination of existing and newly built tracks and stations, with deep-level tunnels constructed through Newcastle city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II_Metro_Bridge" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II Metro Bridge">bridge</a> was built across the Tyne, between Newcastle and Gateshead, and opened by <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> in 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> The network, operated directly by <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Passenger_Transport_Executive" title="Tyne and Wear Passenger Transport Executive">Nexus</a>, carries over 37&#160;million passengers a year,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> extending as far as Newcastle Airport, Tynemouth, <a href="/wiki/South_Shields" title="South Shields">South Shields</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Hylton" title="South Hylton">South Hylton</a> in <a href="/wiki/City_of_Sunderland" title="City of Sunderland">Sunderland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, the company <a href="/wiki/Marconi_Company" title="Marconi Company">Marconi</a> designed and constructed the mobile radio system to the underground Metro system.<sup id="cite_ref-Metromobileradio1_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metromobileradio1-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The Metro system was the first in the UK to have mobile phone antennae installed in the tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-Metromobileradio2_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metromobileradio2-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Metro consists of two lines. The Green line starts at <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Airport_Metro_station" title="Newcastle Airport Metro station">Newcastle Airport</a>, goes through the city centre and into Sunderland, terminating at <a href="/wiki/South_Hylton_Metro_station" title="South Hylton Metro station">South Hylton</a>. The yellow line starts at <a href="/wiki/St_James_Metro_station" title="St James Metro station">St James</a>, runs north of the river alongside Byker towards Whitley Bay, before returning to the city, on to <a href="/wiki/Gateshead_Interchange" title="Gateshead Interchange">Gateshead Interchange</a> and terminates at <a href="/wiki/South_Shields_Metro_station" title="South Shields Metro station">South Shields</a>.
</p><p>The system is currently undergoing a period of refurbishment and modernisation, entitled '<a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro#Current_developments" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Metro: All Change</a>.' The programme has replaced all ticket machines and introduced ticket gates at the busiest stations – part of the transition to smart ticketing. All Metro trains are being completely refurbished and most stations are undergoing improvement works (or in some cases complete reconstruction, for example <a href="/wiki/North_Shields_Metro_station" title="North Shields Metro station">North Shields</a>). In addition; tracks, signalling and overhead wires are also being overhauled.<sup id="cite_ref-Metro2014-2_262-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metro2014-2-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Longer term plans include the procurement of an entirely new fleet of trains and further extensions to the system. Proposed routes include to Newcastle's west end, to the Cobalt business park in North Tyneside, to the Metrocentre in Gateshead and to additional locations in Gateshead, South Tyneside and Sunderland. Several of the proposed routes would require trams as opposed to the current light rail trains.<sup id="cite_ref-Metro2014-1_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metro2014-1-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Major roads in the area include the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1</a> (Gateshead Newcastle Western Bypass), stretching north to <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh" title="Edinburgh">Edinburgh</a> and south to London; the <a href="/wiki/A19_road" title="A19 road">A19</a> heading south past <a href="/wiki/Sunderland,_Tyne_and_Wear" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland, Tyne and Wear">Sunderland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Middlesbrough" title="Middlesbrough">Middlesbrough</a> to <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a> and <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a>; the <a href="/wiki/A69_road" title="A69 road">A69</a> heading west to <a href="/wiki/Carlisle,_Cumbria" class="mw-redirect" title="Carlisle, Cumbria">Carlisle</a>; the <a href="/wiki/A696_road" title="A696 road">A696</a>, which becomes the <a href="/wiki/A68_road" title="A68 road">A68</a> heads past <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Airport" title="Newcastle Airport">Newcastle Airport</a> and up through central <a href="/wiki/Northumberland" title="Northumberland">Northumberland</a> and central <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Borders" title="Scottish Borders">Scottish Borders</a>, the <a href="/wiki/A167_road" title="A167 road">A167</a>, the old "Great North Road", heading south to <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chester-le-Street" title="Chester-le-Street">Chester-le-Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durham,_England" title="Durham, England">Durham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Darlington" title="Darlington">Darlington</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/A1058_road" title="A1058 road">A1058</a> "Coast Road", which runs from <a href="/wiki/Jesmond" title="Jesmond">Jesmond</a> to the east coast between <a href="/wiki/Tynemouth" title="Tynemouth">Tynemouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cullercoats" title="Cullercoats">Cullercoats</a>. Many of these designations are recent—upon completion of the Western Bypass, and its designation as the new line of the A1, the roads between this and the A1's former alignment through the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_Tunnel" title="Tyne Tunnel">Tyne Tunnel</a> were <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_road_numbering_scheme" title="Great Britain road numbering scheme">renumbered</a>, with many city centre roads changing from a 6-prefix<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> to their present 1-prefix numbers. In November 2011 the capacity of the Tyne Tunnel was increased when a project to build a second road tunnel and refurbish the first tunnel was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg/220px-Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg/330px-Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg/440px-Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haymarket_Bus_Station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Haymarket_bus_station" title="Haymarket bus station">Haymarket bus station</a>, one of the city's two main bus stations.</div></div></div>
<p>There are three main bus companies providing services in the city; <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_East" title="Arriva North East">Arriva North East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Go_North_East" title="Go North East">Go North East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_North_East" title="Stagecoach North East">Stagecoach North East</a>. There are two major bus stations in the city: <a href="/wiki/Haymarket_bus_station" title="Haymarket bus station">Haymarket bus station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eldon_Square_bus_station" title="Eldon Square bus station">Eldon Square bus station</a>. Arriva mainly operates from Haymarket bus station providing the majority of services to the north of Newcastle, <a href="/wiki/Northumberland" title="Northumberland">Northumberland</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Tyneside" title="North Tyneside">North Tyneside</a>. Go-Ahead operates from Eldon Square bus station, providing the majority of services south of the river in <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Tyneside" title="South Tyneside">South Tyneside</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunderland,_Tyne_and_Wear" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunderland, Tyne and Wear">Sunderland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/County_Durham" title="County Durham">County Durham</a>. Stagecoach is the primary operator in the city proper, with cross-city services mainly between both the West and East ends via the city centre with some services extending out to the MetroCentre, <a href="/wiki/Killingworth" title="Killingworth">Killingworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wallsend" title="Wallsend">Wallsend</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ponteland" title="Ponteland">Ponteland</a>. Bus services in Newcastle upon Tyne and the surrounding boroughs part of the Tyne &amp; Wear area are coordinated by Nexus, the <a href="/wiki/Tyne_%26_Wear_Passenger_Transport_Executive" class="mw-redirect" title="Tyne &amp; Wear Passenger Transport Executive">Tyne &amp; Wear Passenger Transport Executive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NexusBus_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NexusBus-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Other major departure points are Pilgrim Street for buses running south of the Tyne via <a href="/wiki/Gateshead" title="Gateshead">Gateshead</a>, and Blackett Street/Monument for services to the East or West of the city. Many bus services also pass <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle railway station</a>, a major interchange for rail and metro services.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/QuayLink" title="QuayLink">QuayLink</a> is a bus service operated to the Quayside from Newcastle and Gateshead. <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_coach_station" title="Newcastle coach station">Newcastle coach station</a>, near the railway station, handles long distance bus services operated by <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycle">Cycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Cycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Newcastle is accessible by several mostly traffic-free <a href="/wiki/Cycle_route" class="mw-redirect" title="Cycle route">cycle routes</a> that lead to the edges of the city centre, where cyclists can continue into the city by road, using <a href="/wiki/Bus_lane" title="Bus lane">no car lanes</a>. The traffic-free <a href="/wiki/Sea_to_Sea_Cycle_Route" title="Sea to Sea Cycle Route">C2C</a> cycle route runs along the north bank of the <a href="/wiki/River_Tyne" title="River Tyne">River Tyne</a>, enabling cyclists to travel off-road to <a href="/wiki/North_Shields" title="North Shields">North Shields</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tynemouth" title="Tynemouth">Tynemouth</a> in the east, and westwards towards <a href="/wiki/Hexham" title="Hexham">Hexham</a>.
</p><p>Suburban cycle routes exist, which use converted trackbeds of former industrial <a href="/wiki/Wagonway" title="Wagonway">wagonways</a> and industrial railways. A network on <a href="/wiki/Tyneside" title="Tyneside">Tyneside</a>'s suburban Victorian waggonways is being developed.<sup id="cite_ref-TynesideWaggonways_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TynesideWaggonways-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> A network of signed on-road cycle routes is being established,<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1402-2_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1402-2-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> including some designated on-road cycle lanes that will lead from the city centre to the suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Gosforth" title="Gosforth">Gosforth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heaton,_Newcastle" title="Heaton, Newcastle">Heaton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wallsend" title="Wallsend">Wallsend</a>.
</p><p>Newcastle has a growing culture of bicycle usage. Newcastle is also home to a cycling campaign, called the 'Newcastle Cycling Campaign.'<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1309-1_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1309-1-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The ideal of the organisation is to model other European cities like <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1309-1_270-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1309-1-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> The aims of the organisation, within the constitution are: To raise the profile of cycling, especially utility cycling around the city;<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1309-2_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1309-2-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> to educate decision makers over the benefits of cycling;<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1309-2_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1309-2-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> to promote equality.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1309-2_271-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1309-2-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following guidelines set in the National Cycling strategy, Newcastle first developed its cycling strategy in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1402-1_272-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1402-1-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> As of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the local council social aims and objectives for cycling include: highlighting the usage of cycling to cut city congestion; educating that cycling promotes healthy living…<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1402-2_269-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1402-2-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> The authority also has infrastructure aims and objectives which include: developing on road cycle networks on quieter streets; making safer routes on busier streets; innovating and implementing contraflows on one way streets; developing the existing off-road cycle route networks and improve signage; joining up routes that are partially or completely isolated; Increase the number of cycle parking facilities; working with employers to integrate cycling into workplace travel plans; link the local networks to national networks.<sup id="cite_ref-Newcyc1402-2_269-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newcyc1402-2-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>From Newcastle International Ferry Terminal, at <a href="/wiki/North_Shields" title="North Shields">North Shields</a>, Danish <a href="/wiki/DFDS" title="DFDS">DFDS Seaways</a> runs a service to <a href="/wiki/IJmuiden" title="IJmuiden">IJmuiden</a> (near <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-DFDS_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFDS-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Newcastle%E2%80%93Bergen%E2%80%93Stavanger_ferry" title="Newcastle–Bergen–Stavanger ferry">DFDS ferry service</a> to <a href="/wiki/Gothenburg" title="Gothenburg">Gothenburg</a>, Sweden, ceased at the end of October 2006 and their service to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle%E2%80%93Bergen%E2%80%93Stavanger_ferry" title="Newcastle–Bergen–Stavanger ferry">Bergen and Stavanger</a>, Norway was terminated late 2008. The company cited high fuel prices and new competition from <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost air services</a> as the cause. Since summer 2007, Thomson cruise lines have included Newcastle as a departure port on its Norwegian and Fjords cruise.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg/220px-Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg/330px-Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg/440px-Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2729" data-file-height="1832" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Bridge_Newcastle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Millennium Bridge</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="List of schools in Newcastle Upon Tyne">List of schools in Newcastle Upon Tyne</a></div>
<p>Newcastle has 74 primary schools and 20 secondary school around the city as a whole. There are 13 <a href="/wiki/Local_education_authority" title="Local education authority">LEA</a>-funded and 7 independent schools in Newcastle.
</p><p>There are a number of successful <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">state schools</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Walker_Technology_College" title="Walker Technology College">Walker Technology College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gosforth_High_School" class="mw-redirect" title="Gosforth High School">Gosforth High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heaton_Manor_School" title="Heaton Manor School">Heaton Manor School</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Cuthbert%27s_High_School" title="St Cuthbert&#39;s High School">St Cuthbert's High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Catholic_Comprehensive_School" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Mary&#39;s Catholic Comprehensive School">St. Mary's Catholic Comprehensive School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenton_School" title="Kenton School">Kenton School</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Stephenson_High_School" title="George Stephenson High School">George Stephenson High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_Catholic_High_School_(Newcastle_upon_Tyne)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred Heart Catholic High School (Newcastle upon Tyne)">Sacred Heart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Excelsior_Academy" title="Excelsior Academy">Excelsior Academy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Walbottle_Campus" title="Walbottle Campus">Walbottle Campus</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_School,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Discovery School, Newcastle upon Tyne (page does not exist)">Discovery School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benfield_School" title="Benfield School">Benfield School</a>.
</p><p>The largest <a href="/wiki/Coeducation" class="mw-redirect" title="Coeducation">co-ed</a> independent school is the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Grammar_School,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Royal Grammar School, Newcastle upon Tyne">Royal Grammar School</a>. The largest girls' independent school is <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_High_School_for_Girls" title="Newcastle High School for Girls">Newcastle High School for Girls</a>. Both schools are located on the same street in <a href="/wiki/Jesmond" title="Jesmond">Jesmond</a>. <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_School_for_Boys" title="Newcastle School for Boys">Newcastle School for Boys</a> is the only independent boys' only school in the city and is situated in Gosforth. Other independent schools include <a href="/wiki/Dame_Allan%27s_School,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Dame Allan&#39;s School, Newcastle upon Tyne">Dame Allan's School</a> and <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_College,_Gateshead" title="Emmanuel College, Gateshead">Emmanuel College, Gateshead</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_College" title="Newcastle College">Newcastle College</a> is the largest general <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> college in the North East and is a <a href="/wiki/Beacon_Status" title="Beacon Status">Beacon Status</a> college; there are two smaller colleges in the Newcastle area.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tertiary">Tertiary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Tertiary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg/220px-University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg/330px-University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg/440px-University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Newcastle_Upon_Tyne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Newcastle has one of the country's largest universities for research.</div></div></div>
<p>The city has two universities – <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northumbria_University" title="Northumbria University">Northumbria University</a>. Newcastle University has its origins in the School of Medicine and Surgery, established in 1834 and became independent from <a href="/wiki/Durham_University" title="Durham University">Durham University</a> on 1 August 1963 to form the University of Newcastle upon Tyne. Newcastle University is now one of the UK's leading international universities.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> It won the coveted <a href="/wiki/Sunday_Times_University_of_the_Year" title="Sunday Times University of the Year"><i>Sunday Times</i> University of the Year</a> award in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Northumbria University has its origins in the Newcastle Polytechnic, established in 1969 and became the University of Northumbria at Newcastle in 1992 as part of the UK-wide process in which polytechnics became new universities. Northumbria University was voted 'Best New University' by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> Good University Guide 2005 and also won a much coveted company award of the "Most IT enabled organisation" (in the UK), by the IT industry magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Computing_(magazine)" title="Computing (magazine)">Computing</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_sites">Religious sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Religious sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_upon_Tyne,_England.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Newcastle_upon_Tyne%2C_England.jpg/170px-Newcastle_upon_Tyne%2C_England.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Newcastle_upon_Tyne%2C_England.jpg/255px-Newcastle_upon_Tyne%2C_England.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Newcastle_upon_Tyne%2C_England.jpg/340px-Newcastle_upon_Tyne%2C_England.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Newcastle_upon_Tyne,_England.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Cathedral" title="Newcastle Cathedral">St. Nicholas' Cathedral</a>, as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Castle_Keep" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle Castle Keep">Castle</a></div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Newcastle" title="Diocese of Newcastle">Diocese of Newcastle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Hexham_and_Newcastle" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Hexham and Newcastle">Diocese of Hexham and Newcastle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/North_East_Jewry" class="mw-redirect" title="North East Jewry">North East Jewry</a></div>
<p>Newcastle has three cathedrals, the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Cathedral" title="Newcastle Cathedral">St. Nicholas</a>, with its elegant lantern tower of 1474, the Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Cathedral,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Mary&#39;s Cathedral, Newcastle upon Tyne">St. Mary's</a> designed by <a href="/wiki/Augustus_Welby_Pugin" class="mw-redirect" title="Augustus Welby Pugin">Augustus Welby Pugin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coptic_Orthodox_Church_in_Britain_and_Ireland" title="Coptic Orthodox Church in Britain and Ireland">Coptic Orthodox</a> Cathedral in <a href="/wiki/Fenham" title="Fenham">Fenham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> All three cathedrals began their lives as parish churches. St Mary's became a cathedral in 1850 and St Nicholas' in 1882. Another prominent church in the city centre is the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Thomas_the_Martyr" title="Church of St Thomas the Martyr">Church of St Thomas the Martyr</a> which is the only <a href="/wiki/Parish_church" title="Parish church">parish church</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> without a parish and which is not a <a href="/wiki/Royal_Peculiar" title="Royal Peculiar">peculiar</a>.
</p><p>One of the largest <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">evangelical</a> <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> churches in the UK is <a href="/wiki/Jesmond_Parish_Church" title="Jesmond Parish Church">Jesmond Parish Church</a>, situated a little to the north of the city centre.
</p><p>Newcastle is home to the only <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá&#39;í">Bahá'í</a> Centre in North East England; the centre has served the local Bahá'í community for over 25 years and is located close to the Civic Centre in <a href="/wiki/Jesmond" title="Jesmond">Jesmond</a>.
</p><p>Newcastle was a prominent centre of the <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">Plymouth Brethren</a> movement up to the 1950s, and some small congregations still function. Among these are at the Hall, Denmark Street and Gospel Hall, St Lawrence.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/St_Andrew%27s_Church,_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="St Andrew&#39;s Church, Newcastle upon Tyne">The Parish Church of St Andrew</a> is traditionally recognised as 'the oldest church in this town'.<sup id="cite_ref-oldparish12012_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oldparish12012-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> The present building was begun in the 12th Century and the last addition to it, apart from the vestries, was the main porch in 1726.<sup id="cite_ref-oldparish22012_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oldparish22012-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> It is quite possible that there was an earlier church here dating from Saxon times. This older church would have been one of several churches along the River Tyne dedicated to St Andrew, including the <a href="/wiki/Hexham_Abbey" title="Hexham Abbey">Priory church</a> at Hexham.<sup id="cite_ref-oldparish22012_281-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oldparish22012-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> The building contains more old stonework than any other church in Newcastle. It is surrounded by the last of the ancient churchyards to retain its original character. Many key names associated with Newcastle's history worshipped and were buried here. The church tower received a battering during the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Newcastle_upon_Tyne#Stuart_period" title="History of Newcastle upon Tyne">Siege of Newcastle</a> by the Scots who finally breached the Town Wall and forced surrender. Three of the cannonballs remain on site as testament to the siege.<sup id="cite_ref-oldparish22012_281-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oldparish22012-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_television_shows_set_in_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="List of television shows set in Newcastle upon Tyne">List of television shows set in Newcastle upon Tyne</a></div>
<p>Local newspapers that are printed in Newcastle include <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Mirror" class="mw-redirect" title="Trinity Mirror">Trinity Mirror</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Evening_Chronicle" title="Evening Chronicle">Evening Chronicle</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Journal_(newspaper)" title="The Journal (newspaper)">The Journal</a></i>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Sunday_Sun" title="Sunday Sun">Sunday Sun</a></i> as well as the <i><a href="/wiki/Metro_(British_newspaper)" title="Metro (British newspaper)">Metro</a></i> freesheet. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Crack_(magazine)" title="The Crack (magazine)">The Crack</a></i> is a monthly style and <a href="/wiki/Listings_magazine" title="Listings magazine">listings magazine</a> similar to London's <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Out_(magazine)" title="Time Out (magazine)">Time Out</a></i>. The adult comic <i><a href="/wiki/Viz_(comic)" class="mw-redirect" title="Viz (comic)">Viz</a></i> originated in Jesmond and includes many references to Newcastle, and <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Mag_(sports_magazine)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Mag (sports magazine) (page does not exist)">The Mag</a></i> is a fanzine for Newcastle United supporters.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tyne_Tees,_City_Road.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tyne_Tees%2C_City_Road.jpg/220px-Tyne_Tees%2C_City_Road.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tyne_Tees%2C_City_Road.jpg/330px-Tyne_Tees%2C_City_Road.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Tyne_Tees%2C_City_Road.jpg/440px-Tyne_Tees%2C_City_Road.jpg 2x" data-file-width="925" data-file-height="740" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tyne_Tees,_City_Road.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two converted warehouses provided the base for Tyne Tees on City Road until 2005</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/ITV_Tyne_Tees" title="ITV Tyne Tees">ITV Tyne Tees</a> was based at City Road for over 40 years after its launch in January 1959.<sup id="cite_ref-crs_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crs-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> In 2005 it moved to a new facility on The Watermark business park next to the MetroCentre in Gateshead.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup> The entrance to studio 5 at the City Road complex gave its name to the 1980s music television programme, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tube_(TV_series)" title="The Tube (TV series)">The Tube</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-crs_282-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-crs-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_East_and_Cumbria" title="BBC North East and Cumbria">BBC North East and Cumbria</a> is located to the north of the city on Barrack Road, <a href="/wiki/Spital_Tongues" title="Spital Tongues">Spital Tongues</a>, in a building known, as the result of its colouring, as the Pink Palace.<sup id="cite_ref-pink_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pink-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> It is from here that the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">Corporation</a> broadcasts the <i><a href="/wiki/BBC_Look_North_(North_East_and_Cumbria)" title="BBC Look North (North East and Cumbria)">Look North</a></i> television regional news programme and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Local_Radio" title="BBC Local Radio">local radio</a> station <a href="/wiki/BBC_Newcastle" title="BBC Newcastle">BBC Newcastle</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Independent_Local_Radio" title="Independent Local Radio">Independent Local Radio</a> stations include <a href="/wiki/Metro_Radio" title="Metro Radio">Metro Radio</a> and sister station <a href="/wiki/Metro_2_Radio" title="Metro 2 Radio">Metro 2 Radio</a>, which are both based in a building on the Swan House roundabout on the north side of the Tyne Bridge. <a href="/wiki/Capital_North_East" title="Capital North East">Capital North East</a> broadcasts across Newcastle from its studios in nearby <a href="/wiki/Wallsend" title="Wallsend">Wallsend</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Heart_North_East" title="Heart North East">Heart North East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smooth_North_East" title="Smooth North East">Smooth North East</a> both broadcast from <a href="/wiki/Team_Valley" title="Team Valley">Team Valley</a> in Gateshead.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/NE1fm" title="NE1fm">NE1fm</a> launched on 8 June 2007, the first full-time <a href="/wiki/Community_radio" title="Community radio">community radio</a> station in the area.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_Student_Radio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Newcastle Student Radio (page does not exist)">Newcastle Student Radio</a> is run by students from both of the city's universities, broadcasting from <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University_Union_Society" class="mw-redirect" title="Newcastle University Union Society">students' union building</a> during term time.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> Radio Tyneside<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup> has been the voluntary <a href="/wiki/Hospital_radio" title="Hospital radio">hospital radio</a> service for most hospitals across Newcastle and Gateshead since 1951, broadcasting on <a href="/wiki/Hospedia" title="Hospedia">Hospedia</a>
<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> and online.
The city also has a Radio Lollipop station based at the Great North Children's Hospital in the Newcastle <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Infirmary" title="Royal Victoria Infirmary">Royal Victoria Infirmary</a>.
</p><p>Newcastle is one of the first in the UK to have its city centre covered by <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">wireless internet</a> access. It was developed and installed at the end of 2006 and went active in March 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_residents_of_Newcastle_upon_Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="List of residents of Newcastle upon Tyne">List of residents of Newcastle upon Tyne</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Charles_Avison" title="Charles Avison">Charles Avison</a>, the leading British composer of concertos in the 18th century, was born in Newcastle upon Tyne in 1709 and died there in 1770.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Basil_Hume" title="Basil Hume">Basil Hume</a>, <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Westminster" title="Archbishop of Westminster">Archbishop of Westminster</a>, was born in the city in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup> Vice Admiral <a href="/wiki/Cuthbert_Collingwood,_1st_Baron_Collingwood" title="Cuthbert Collingwood, 1st Baron Collingwood">Cuthbert Collingwood</a>, 1st Baron Collingwood, was born in the city. <a href="/wiki/Ironmaster" title="Ironmaster">Ironmaster</a>, metallurgist, and member of parliament <a href="/wiki/Sir_Lowthian_Bell,_1st_Baronet" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Lowthian Bell, 1st Baronet">Isaac Lowthian Bell</a> was born in the city in 1816. Other notable people born in or associated with Newcastle include: engineer and industrialist <a href="/wiki/William_George_Armstrong,_1st_Baron_Armstrong" class="mw-redirect" title="William George Armstrong, 1st Baron Armstrong">Lord Armstrong</a>, engineer and father of the modern steam railways <a href="/wiki/George_Stephenson" title="George Stephenson">George Stephenson</a>, his son, also an engineer, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Stephenson" title="Robert Stephenson">Robert Stephenson</a>, engineer and inventor of the steam turbine <a href="/wiki/Sir_Charles_Parsons" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Charles Parsons">Sir Charles Parsons</a>, inventor of the incandescent light bulb <a href="/wiki/Sir_Joseph_Swan" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Joseph Swan">Sir Joseph Swan</a>, modernist poet <a href="/wiki/Basil_Bunting" title="Basil Bunting">Basil Bunting</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> and Lord Chief Justice <a href="/wiki/Peter_Taylor,_Baron_Taylor_of_Gosforth" title="Peter Taylor, Baron Taylor of Gosforth">Peter Taylor</a>. Portuguese writer <a href="/wiki/E%C3%A7a_de_Queiroz" class="mw-redirect" title="Eça de Queiroz">Eça de Queiroz</a> was a diplomat in Newcastle from late 1874 until April 1879—his most productive literary period.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> Former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Thailand" title="Prime Minister of Thailand">Prime Minister of Thailand</a> <a href="/wiki/Abhisit_Vejjajiva" title="Abhisit Vejjajiva">Abhisit Vejjajiva</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> was born in the city. Composer <a href="/wiki/Agust%C3%ADn_Fern%C3%A1ndez_S%C3%A1nchez" class="mw-redirect" title="Agustín Fernández Sánchez">Agustín Fernández</a> has been based in the city since 1995, teaching at <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a> and occasionally collaborating with <a href="/wiki/Royal_Northern_Sinfonia" title="Royal Northern Sinfonia">Royal Northern Sinfonia</a>.
</p><p>Musicians <a href="/wiki/Cheryl_(singer)" title="Cheryl (singer)">Cheryl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eric_Burdon" title="Eric Burdon">Eric Burdon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Knopfler" title="Mark Knopfler">Mark Knopfler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Dunn" title="Jeffrey Dunn">Jeffrey Dunn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brian_Johnson" title="Brian Johnson">Brian Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alan_Hull" title="Alan Hull">Alan Hull</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Neil_Tennant" title="Neil Tennant">Neil Tennant</a> lived in Newcastle. <a href="/wiki/Hank_Marvin" title="Hank Marvin">Hank Marvin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Welch" title="Bruce Welch">Bruce Welch</a> were both former pupils of Rutherford Grammar School,<sup id="cite_ref-MarvWelch2007_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarvWelch2007-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup> actors <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Hunnam" title="Charlie Hunnam">Charlie Hunnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Scott_(actor)" title="James Scott (actor)">James Scott</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> entertainers <a href="/wiki/Ant_%26_Dec" title="Ant &amp; Dec">Ant &amp; Dec</a> and international footballers <a href="/wiki/Michael_Carrick" title="Michael Carrick">Michael Carrick</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a> were born in Newcastle. Multiple circumnavigator <a href="/wiki/David_Scott_Cowper" title="David Scott Cowper">David Scott Cowper</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_in_Physics" title="List of Nobel laureates in Physics">Nobel Prize winning physicist</a> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Higgs" title="Peter Higgs">Peter Higgs</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Higgs201310_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Higgs201310-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Neville" class="mw-redirect" title="Adrian Neville">Neville</a> were born in the city. <a href="/wiki/John_Dunn_(bagpipe_maker)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Dunn (bagpipe maker)">John Dunn</a>, inventor of keyed <a href="/wiki/Northumbrian_smallpipes" title="Northumbrian smallpipes">Northumbrian smallpipes</a>, the most characteristic musical instrument in the region, lived and worked in the city. <a href="/wiki/Kathryn_Tickell" title="Kathryn Tickell">Kathryn Tickell</a> OBE, the celebrated Northumbrian piper and composer, has longstanding associations with Newcastle as a resident, frequent performer at <a href="/wiki/Sage_Gateshead" title="Sage Gateshead">Sage Gateshead</a> and teacher at <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_University" title="Newcastle University">Newcastle University</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Marc_Smith_(palaeographer)" title="Marc Smith (palaeographer)">Marc Smith (palaeographer)</a> (born 1963), French palaeographer, was born in Newcastle upon Tyne. One half of <a href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Got_Talent" title="Britain&#39;s Got Talent">Britain's Got Talent</a> impressionist double act The Mimic Men, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cal_Halbert&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Cal Halbert (page does not exist)">Cal Halbert</a>, lives in Newcastle after relocating from his hometown of <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury" title="Shrewsbury">Shrewsbury</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Freddy_Shepherd" title="Freddy Shepherd">Freddy Shepherd</a> was chairman of <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United F.C.</a> for ten years, and died at home in <a href="/wiki/Jesmond" title="Jesmond">Jesmond</a>.
</p>

<p>A large majority of the <a href="/wiki/Geordie_Shore" title="Geordie Shore">Geordie Shore</a> cast were born and reside in Newcastle. They include <a href="/wiki/Marty_McKenna" title="Marty McKenna">Marty McKenna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chloe_Ferry" title="Chloe Ferry">Chloe Ferry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zahida_Allen" title="Zahida Allen">Zahida Allen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Crosby" title="Charlotte Crosby">Charlotte Crosby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicky_Pattison" title="Vicky Pattison">Vicky Pattison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Holly_Hagan" title="Holly Hagan">Holly Hagan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marnie_Simpson" title="Marnie Simpson">Marnie Simpson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaz_Beadle" title="Gaz Beadle">Gaz Beadle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sarah_Goodhart" title="Sarah Goodhart">Sarah Goodhart</a>, Nathan Henry, <a href="/wiki/Scotty_T" title="Scotty T">Scotty T</a> and Sophie Kasaei.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Twin_towns_.E2.80.93_Sister_cities"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_–_Sister_cities">Twin towns – Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Twin towns – Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_friendship_agreements">Other friendship agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Other friendship agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Newcastle also has a "friendship agreement" with
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Little_Rock,_Arkansas" title="Little Rock, Arkansas">Little Rock</a>, United States.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>and, since 2003, a "special cooperation agreement" with
</p>
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden"><img alt="Sweden" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malmö">Malmö</a>, Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-Malmö_twinning_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Malmö_twinning-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Newcastle was part of the 1998 <a href="/wiki/Summit_(meeting)" title="Summit (meeting)">summit</a> of worldwide <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Newcastle (disambiguation)">cities named "New Castle"</a> with:
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 18em; -webkit-column-width: 18em; column-width: 18em;"><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Neuburg_an_der_Donau" title="Neuburg an der Donau">Neuburg an der Donau</a> Germany
<p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland"><img alt="Switzerland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/16px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png" width="16" height="16" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/24px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Switzerland.svg/32px-Flag_of_Switzerland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Neuch%C3%A2tel" title="Neuchâtel">Neuchâtel</a> Switzerland
</p><p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Neufch%C3%A2teau,_Vosges" title="Neufchâteau, Vosges">Neufchâteau</a> France
</p><p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Indiana" title="New Castle, Indiana">New Castle, Indiana</a> USA
</p><p><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States"><img alt="United States" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/New_Castle,_Pennsylvania" title="New Castle, Pennsylvania">New Castle, Pennsylvania</a> USA

<span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa"><img alt="South Africa" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/23px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/35px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Flag_of_South_Africa.svg/45px-Flag_of_South_Africa.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Newcastle,_KwaZulu-Natal" title="Newcastle, KwaZulu-Natal">Newcastle, KwaZulu-Natal</a> South Africa</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_consulates">Foreign consulates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Newcastle_upon_Tyne&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Foreign consulates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The following countries have <a href="/wiki/Consulate" class="mw-redirect" title="Consulate">consular representation</a> in Newcastle: Denmark,<sup id="cite_ref-newcDenmark201802_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newcDenmark201802-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> Finland, Romania,
Belgium,<sup id="cite_ref-belgium21512_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-belgium21512-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> France,<sup id="cite_ref-france21512_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-france21512-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-germany21512_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-germany21512-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> Iceland,<sup id="cite_ref-Iceland21412_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Iceland21412-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> Italy,<sup id="cite_ref-Italy21512_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Italy21512-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> Norway,<sup id="cite_ref-Norway21512_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norway21512-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> and Sweden.<sup id="cite_ref-sweden21512_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sweden21512-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
